  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_109f83ab-7f5d-47ca-ab0a-97a6293a0b72'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think you ought to read Cinder, Scarlet, and Cress first. You'll be more familiar with the characters that seem to be only mentioned a few times in <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think you ought to read Cinder, Scarlet, and Cress first. You'll be more familiar with the characters that seem to be only mentioned a few times in this book (haven't read it yet) and may get the wrong idea about Queen Levena. She's evil!!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_1557593066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1557593066" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1557593066?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1557593066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10768399442514169091"><blockquote>
  <i>“She cried for the girl who had never belonged. A girl who tried so hard, harder than anyone else, and still never had anything to show for it.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>4 1/2 stars. This is <b>easily my favourite book of the series</b>. Well... so far, but I find it hard to imagine that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_' title='Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Winter</a> will top this.<br/><br/>I enjoyed this book immensely and I had the feeling beforehand that it would be the villain's story that affected me most. There's just something really great about reading the stories behind the villains, finding out w</span>
  <span id="freeText10768399442514169091" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“She cried for the girl who had never belonged. A girl who tried so hard, harder than anyone else, and still never had anything to show for it.”</i>
</blockquote><br />4 1/2 stars. This is <b>easily my favourite book of the series</b>. Well... so far, but I find it hard to imagine that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_" title="Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter</a> will top this.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book immensely and I had the feeling beforehand that it would be the villain's story that affected me most. There's just something really great about reading the stories behind the villains, finding out why they became the way they are. <br /><br />Levana is a seriously crazy bitch in the other books of the Lunar Chronicles. It personally made me want to know more about her. For me, a complex villain with a backstory that can create sympathy is one of the strongest kinds of characters. Better than any tough heroine or dreamy love interest.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe the princess could save herself."<br />"That sounds like a pretty good story too.”</i>
</blockquote><br />This book doesn't actually take away any of the crazy, evil villainy from Levana, but it does offer convincing (and seriously disturbing) reasons as to why she became the way she is. You still don't like her, you still know she is batshit crazy, and yet there is something so sad and tragic about this story.<br /><br />Young Levana is smart, ambitious, and desperately in need of love that she never got from her parents or sister. I'm glad that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22489107.Fairest__The_Lunar_Chronicles___3_5_" title="Fairest (The Lunar Chronicles, #3.5) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a> doesn't linger too long on the pity party; if it had, it would probably have felt contrived and manipulative. Instead, Levana quickly grows both cruel and controlling, fuelling the reader's dislike but also leaving behind a sad, bitter aftertaste.<br /><br /><b>Things could have been so different</b>.<br /><br />I'm really looking forward to reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_" title="Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter</a>, but part of me also hopes that Meyer will return to spin-off novellas. If they are anything like this one, they'll pack a short, emotional punch.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10768399442514169091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a style="font-weight:bold" href="/user/show/15850736-hannah-papernick-yudin">Hannah Papernick-yudin</a>

      
<span id="freeTextContainer16595004587905389037">I agree there were some very powerful and even bone-chilling quotes in this book. Especially when Levana was looking at baby Winter through the window</span>
  <span id="freeText16595004587905389037" style="display:none">I agree there were some very powerful and even bone-chilling quotes in this book. Especially when Levana was looking at baby Winter through the window of the baby ward when she suddenly caught her reflection and was disturbed into losing control of her glamour; the fact that she had to shove the image out of her mind while hiding her face from everyone until she called the glamour back up is just super dark; I felt her fear of mirrors to a point where I've dreamed of being in her situation, catching my reflection in windows and fearing it, expecting to see Levana's disfigurements and one eye being sealed shut...<br />Her story is HEARTBREAKING, and the subtle commentary on the royal family truly captures how Channery and especially Levana lacked the nurturing of their parents; I always imagine how the king and queen must have reacted when Levana was disfigured, or did they even care..? The idea of her father and sister caring only to marry her off and not about the disfigurements she has been forced to hide with glamour is disturbing as all hell.<br />I seriously couldn't get enough of this book; it's almost criminal that it isn't longer.</span>

<div id="review_2252840818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2252840818" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2252840818?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall">2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2252840818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9582938293566187657"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605968391i/30408429._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Seven of my favorite Bookish Villains in one <b><u><a href='https://youtu.be/sAaQkvGPGag' rel='nofollow noopener'>BookTube Video</a></u></b>!</blockquote><b>Onwards to the written review!<b><u>The Written Review</u></b><br/><br/><b>An absolutely essential read.</b><br/><br/>Rarely (and I do mean<b><i> rarely</i></b>) does a companion novel enhance, improve and brings another dimension the original set. <b> Fairest does all that and more.</b><br/><br/>Lunars (the advanced civilization living on the moon) can manipulate what you see and think through bioelectric energy. <br/><br/>Princess Levana (age 15) is neurotic about maintaining her glamour at all times due to a <b>disf</b></b></span>
  <span id="freeText9582938293566187657" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605968391i/30408429._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seven of my favorite Bookish Villains in one <b><u><a href="https://youtu.be/sAaQkvGPGag" rel="nofollow noopener">BookTube Video</a></u></b>!</blockquote><b>Onwards to the written review!<b><u>The Written Review</u></b><br><br><b>An absolutely essential read.</b><br><br>Rarely (and I do mean<b><i> rarely</i></b>) does a companion novel enhance, improve and brings another dimension the original set. <b> Fairest does all that and more.</b><br><br>Lunars (the advanced civilization living on the moon) can manipulate what you see and think through bioelectric energy. <br><br>Princess Levana (age 15) is neurotic about maintaining her glamour at all times due to a <b>disfiguring "accident"</b> caused by her older sister, Channery, a decade ago. <br><br>Through tantalizing tidbits, we learn that Levana was <b>manipulated, bullied and tortured</b> by her sister for years. And by manipulated, that includes using the bioelectric kind.<br><br>Through whispered conversations, the audience learns that it is forbidden to bioelectrically manipulate children because the bioelectrics directly affect their growing brains -<b> producing disastrous side-effects. </b><br><br>Almost without realizing it, Levana soon starts displaying those side-effects. <blockquote><i> This was the part that Levana could not figure out. How did you kill a child? There were so many possibilities...</i></blockquote> When their parents die, Channery is crowned queen and all Levana can think is <b>how she could do it better</b>. And when Channery <b><i>mysteriously dies, </i></b>Levana finally gets that chance. <blockquote><i>No matter what anyone thought, she was the fairest queen Luna had ever known.</i></blockquote>And she <i>was</i> right - she's so much better at being a queen than her sister ever could be. Only, Channery left behind a heir (Cinder) and that <b>just simply would not do. </b> <br><br>Levana seemed like such a<b> shallow, evil "big bad"</b> in books one to three, but now I get her. This book really delved into her motives and brought her to life as a fully realized three-dimensional being.<br><br>Levana is a <b>deliciously evil character</b> through and through - and while this book is not necessary to understand the original quartet, it certainly brings new light to the veiled villain.<br><br> I appreciated that while this book <b>brought sympathy to a rather unsympathetic character</b>, it did not turn her into a misunderstood anti-hero.<br><br><b> Audiobook Comments</b><br>--Well read. Whenever Rebecca Soler said, "Come here baby sister" I got chills!<br><br>If you are curious about Rebecca Soler, check Tucker the Reader's <a href="https://tuckerthereader.wordpress.com/2019/04/30/interview-with-rebecca-soler/" rel="nofollow noopener"> interview</a>!<br><br><i>The Finer Books Club - 2018 Reading Challenge: A book with a one-word title</i><br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9582938293566187657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7255260940279907630">Book 24/100 of 2015<br/><br/>WOW SO GOOD! I really shouldn't like nor sympathize with Levana, kind of made me! Well...not exactly <i>like</i>, but definitely understand who she is and why she ended up that way. The pacing was great and I was never bored, which should be expected as it is only 222 pages. I also liked that we got a whole backstory for Cinder and Winter as well! I CAN'T WAIT UNTIL WINTER IS RELEASED</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10119365275382314952"><i>Buddy read with amazing<b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com' rel='nofollow noopener'> Tanya</a> (:</b></i><br/><br/>YES.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402942204ra/10016432.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>_________________<br/> <br/><br/><p>When I decided to read this book, I did it having in mind every other book in this series: funny, compelling and perfectly okay stories. That would explain why<b> I was really not expecting the level of creepiness, weirdness and are-you-fucking-kidding-me-ness </b>this book had to offer.<br/><br/></p><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>She hated mirrors. Hated their reflections, their truths.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423023647i/13577763._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Among Meyer's characters, Levana is definelty the most complex one. I could easily describe the </span>
  <span id="freeText10119365275382314952" style="display:none"><i>Buddy read with amazing<b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tanya</a> (:</b></i><br><br>YES.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402942204ra/10016432.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>_________________<br> <br><br><p>When I decided to read this book, I did it having in mind every other book in this series: funny, compelling and perfectly okay stories. That would explain why<b> I was really not expecting the level of creepiness, weirdness and are-you-fucking-kidding-me-ness </b>this book had to offer.<br><br></p><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>She hated mirrors. Hated their reflections, their truths.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423023647i/13577763._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Among Meyer's characters, Levana is definelty the most complex one. I could easily describe the evil queen as a psycho and still there would be plenty unsaid. <br><br><b>When it comes to villains, I can deal with evil. I'm not sure I was ready for mental illness, </b>genius move, everybody. We're given free pass to Levana's head and trust me, it's not a comfortable place to be. She's insecure, pitiful, broken and completely alone and even if I didn't sympathize with her, I think I felt sorry for her in an almost<i> I hope you die</i> kinda way.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422859963ra/13555293.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I must say<b> I'm grateful it wasn't about understanding Levana and eventually sympathizing with her.</b> I was not in the mood to like her, I wanted a real villain. It was actually a surprise to read about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Levana losing her virginity and forcing a man to sleep with her,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> being this YA and all. <br><br>It was very well executed and I approve this book for the little ones (it's not a secret I'm my sister's Book Police and I try to protect her from the evil world out there). I felt it was too short or maybe the ending was too abrupt and, as Tanya was saying,<b> it's a shame we don't get to see the cold blooded bitch queen we've come to know and love</b> but just the immature and infatuated little girl longing for love. I feel so sorry for Evret and Winter, but now can't wait for book #4! Another OTP is near.<br><br><i>Note: Don't read this story unless you've read till book #3. It's barely spoilery but I think you won't enjoy it as much unless you get to know some of the characters first.</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer968863200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5264710670652774980"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/01/review-fairest-by-marissa-meyer.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>It didn't occur to me that some readers might skip this installment of THE LUNAR CHRONICLES, counting it as a novella. Technically, while being a prequel, I think it's still a full-length novel. I don't know the word count, but I did the math (with a calculator, and everything), and even excluding the preview of WINTER that begins at 79%, Levana's story is still over 200 pages.<br/><br/>FYI.<br/><br/>And regardless, any fan of the series will want to read this book, b/c:<br/><br/>1. What does Levana r</span>
  <span id="freeText5264710670652774980" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/01/review-fairest-by-marissa-meyer.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>It didn't occur to me that some readers might skip this installment of THE LUNAR CHRONICLES, counting it as a novella. Technically, while being a prequel, I think it's still a full-length novel. I don't know the word count, but I did the math (with a calculator, and everything), and even excluding the preview of WINTER that begins at 79%, Levana's story is still over 200 pages.<br><br>FYI.<br><br>And regardless, any fan of the series will want to read this book, b/c:<br><br>1. What does Levana really look like under that veil?<br><br>2. What happened to Levana's husband, and how did Winter end up in her care?<br><br>3. What is the depth of Levana's evil?<br><br>And those are just a few of the questions that FAIREST answers.<br><br>Also . . . as it turns out, Levana might just be as crazy as she is nefarious. The end result is the same, of course, but I was surprised. If she was simply a narcissist, I might not have been, and that's definitely part of the crazy, but guys . . . this woman is diabolically <i>insane</i>.<br><br>It's uncomfortable.<br><br>I had the misfortune of agreeing with my husband to PILLARS OF THE EARTH as our holiday driving read this year . . . I loathed it. And for once I didn't have to analyze what it was that made me loathe it: there are just some people's heads you don't want to be inside of. <br><br>Clearly, I didn't hate FAIREST, but sharing Levana's headspace is . . . well, it's stressful, I was full of stress. And awkward. I don't think I'd like to see a picture of myself while I was reading, b/c I'm pretty sure if my face wasn't stuck in perpetual grimace, my eyebrows were at my hairline with my eyes bugging out of my head, b/c WTF?<br><blockquote>
  <i>Levana had not seen the bodies, but she had seen the bedrooms the next morning, and her first thought was that all that blood would make a very pretty rouge on her lips.</i>
</blockquote><br>Those bodies? Yeah, they were her PARENTS. Her parents who had been MURDERED. And that is the least of it. <br><br>In addition to finding out what's going on under that veil, you also find out <em>why</em> she choose the specific glamour she uses . . . and it is . . . W-H-O-A (and I'm totally making that face again). <br><br>Are there reasons for the CRAY?<br><br>Oh yeah. And you learn those too. <br><br>Did it make Levana a more sympathetic character?<br><br>NOPE. Not to me, anyway. Just like Channary (Cinder's mother) wasn't made a more sympathetic character b/c she showed a few surprisingly maternal instincts. <br><br>Am I a hardass? Maybe. Probably. But I've said it before, and I'll say it again: it's not what you've been through, it's how you handle it that matters, and I have a sneaking suspicion that even without the crazy (b/c Bad Things), Levana would still be diabolical. <br><br>Overall, FAIREST paints an unambiguous portrait of the most vile villain to ever plague (HA!)both Lunars and Earthens. It cleverly weaves together multiple threads from the characters that readers have grown to know and love in previous installments of THE LUNAR CHRONICLES, and reveals, step-by-murderous-and-entitled-step, how Levana and her immediate family have sown the seeds of their own inevitable downfall. Highly recommended. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/472888024" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Glitches (Lunar Chronicles 0.5)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351598724" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/472888512" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen's Army (Lunar Chronicles, #1.5)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/403256586" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet (The Lunar Chronicles, #2)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/529142847" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Cress (The Lunar Chronicles, #3)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/838071872" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4)</a>

  <span id="freeText15072592049266785869" style="display:none"><blockquote>

ALL authors are bullies, pass it on.<br><br>before reading this book i used to compare levana to donald trump and honestly i take it all back bc even tho trump is a psycho bitch too he's got <i>nothing</i> on levana (my apologies, sir) even though they both have in common that they're a pretty big <b>threat on planet Earth</b> lmao <br><br>anyways, i feel like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/183660.Fairest" title="Fairest by Gail Carson Levine" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a> is the embodiment of the phrase "don't ever judge a person before you really get to know them", because we all fight battles no one knows about and levana is really just a tortured soul like all of us................................jk i still hate her bye<br><br><b>!!!: SPOILER WARNING</b><br><br><u>Reasons why levana is the #1 psycho bitch and also all of this fucked me up:</u><br><br>• she tried to SET A BABY ON FIRE<br>• she also fantasized about torturing said baby for,, years probably<br>• she tried not to smile during basically all funerals she ever attended like o....kayyyy........... psychopath<br>• she literally mind-raped a guy at the mere age of 16!!! years (at that age i was still playing with Legos probably)<br>• she forced someone to love her with mind-control (lmao me actually) for 10 YEARS <br><br>i can't believe all of this is canon....... i have to lay down for a bit.................. think about the fact that we can all be very grateful that we were not born as Marissa Meyer characters........................ imagine having Channary as sister *shudders*<br><br><blockquote>

<div id="review_1149803926" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149803926" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12842423-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539992905p2/12842423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1149803926?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/12842423-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1149803926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9839483177988218268">Full Review on YouTube: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/RAd1c5jKxA8'>https://youtu.be/RAd1c5jKxA8</a><br/><br/>Yikes. This queen is cray...<br/><br/>We all knew that Queen Levana was a bit psycho from reading Cinder, Scarlet, and Cress... I never realized how many issues this lady really has. <br/>I LOVED this book, just like the other books in the Lunar Chronicles. If you haven't read this series yet, I would suggest that you don't start with this book, however. I know that it's a prequel, but so much information is shared in this book that you don't learn until book</span>
  <span id="freeText9839483177988218268" style="display:none">Full Review on YouTube: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/RAd1c5jKxA8">https://youtu.be/RAd1c5jKxA8</a><br /><br />Yikes. This queen is cray...<br /><br />We all knew that Queen Levana was a bit psycho from reading Cinder, Scarlet, and Cress... I never realized how many issues this lady really has. <br />I LOVED this book, just like the other books in the Lunar Chronicles. If you haven't read this series yet, I would suggest that you don't start with this book, however. I know that it's a prequel, but so much information is shared in this book that you don't learn until book three in this series. I guess you CAN start with this one, and you'll just be really informed while reading the series, but I wouldn't suggest it. I think it will take away a lot and you'll enjoy the series a lot more if you read books 1-3 before this one!<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I understand that Levana is scared (on the inside and outside) and that's greatly changed who she is. I understand that she's lonely and has never really felt loved before. But that still doesn't excuse her insane actions. <br /><br />When I first started this, I kind of forgot that Levena must have been married before since Winter is her stepdaughter. I knew that her crush on Evert was so hopeless that they would never marry. I DEFINITELY never thought that Levana would control him to marry her. Has she no pride at all? She had to control him for every single kiss. It was honestly so creepy that she would glamour herself as Solstice. <br /><br />I thought that it was really ironic that she kept saying things like, "she would never be like her sister... if SHE was Queen, she would do this, this, and this..." Although her sister wasn't perfect herself (I mean she burned her six year old little sister, and cut the feet off of her seamstress...) I still think in some ways she may have been a better Queen than Levana. Channary would have continued to just focus on boys and parties, while her council would have made most of the decisions. Levana on the other hand, continued to increase production although she was told that Luna couldn't sustain it. They would eventually completely run out of resources. We all know what kind of Queen Levana has turned out to be.. and I don't think her sister could have been any worse. In fact, towards the end of her life, at 25, I think she was starting to grow out of some of her cruelness. The way she acted towards her daughter really showed that maybe she wasn't all that bad...<br /><br />Many of you will agree with me that one of the worst parts was hearing Levana plot to kill Princess Selene/Cinder. I understand that she was threatened by her, but really? And the WAY that she did it. When she first started thinking about murdering her, she wanted to make sure it was as painless as possible. Then ultimately decided to just burn her to death. Ya, that's real painless. Good job Levana. I can't believe that she would make someone else suffer what she went through, but worse, and at that age.<br /><br />Poor, poor Evert. He was just one unlucky guy that happened to catch an evil Princess's eye. I honestly don't think that there was anything he could have done. I think anything he did was going to ultimately end up with him being murdered by Levana. Whether he refused her, ran, whatever he did. I can't believe he went from being married to one of the nicest women in the world to LEVANA. Poor chap...<br /><br />When Queen Channary was talking about her daughter and how many she could marry the Emperor's son I was freaking out! Kai and Cinder!! So ironic that Cinder's mom had already thought of their marriage...<br /><br />When Winter and her father were reading the children's story, and she goes, "Why does the Prince always save the Princess? Why not a doctor?" I thought that was also pretty cool because Dr. Erland was the one that saved Princess Selene/Cinder. Then later Winter mentions that the Princess should just save herself... and that's kind of what Cinder is now doing!<br /><br />Why do you guys think that Levana ruined Winter's face? I was surprised that part wasn't in this book... I think it goes beyond her just being jealous of how beautiful she was. I think that every time she saw Winter, she saw the man that she murdered that never loved her. She saw Solstice, the simple, but beautiful woman that Levana could never beat.<br /><br />I'm really, really excited to read Winter now! I hope that Winter and Princess Selene/Cinder team up to bring Levana down together since she took so much from both of them.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />What did you guys think of the book?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9839483177988218268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1354779723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4675027987723517452">Okay so I knew I didn't like this book, but I didn't know I <i>hated</i> it.<br/><br/>Life is just full of surprises.<br/><br/>I like Levana as a villain in the real Lunar Chronicles books (I am already actively removing this from my conception of the series) because a b*tch is RUTHLESS. She is kicking ass and taking names and committing acts of biological warfare that lead to long-term genocide.<br/><br/>Your fave fantasy villain could never.<br/><br/>She's also crafty and smart and mysterious and all of that is what makes her cool as hell.</span>
  <span id="freeText4675027987723517452" style="display:none">Okay so I knew I didn't like this book, but I didn't know I <i>hated</i> it.<br /><br />Life is just full of surprises.<br /><br />I like Levana as a villain in the real Lunar Chronicles books (I am already actively removing this from my conception of the series) because a b*tch is RUTHLESS. She is kicking ass and taking names and committing acts of biological warfare that lead to long-term genocide.<br /><br />Your fave fantasy villain could never.<br /><br />She's also crafty and smart and mysterious and all of that is what makes her cool as hell. <br /><br />I also think it's unbearably lame when villains are given ~backstories~ and ~emotions~ and are made ~sympathetic~. Gross. Who wants realistic, emotive characters in 2018? Who wants to <i>feel</i> emotions in 2018? We stan constantly scheming, purely cruel female villains o n l y.<br /><br />So I was prepared from the get-go not to like this book, which promises to explain why Levana is the way she is and depict her as a person or whatever. My nightmare. <br /><br />But also this was worse than I possibly could have imagined.<br /><br />This does a very bad job of explaining why Levana is the way she is or making her seem like a person at all. From the very beginning of this book, she is manipulative and entitled and creepy and awful. This entire story made me so uncomfortable. Rather than being a villain before she was a villain, Levana is a literal sexual harasser who uses her powers to emotionally and sexually abuse the guy she """loves."""<br /><br />There is just so much that is wrong with this. Every page was hard to get through.<br /><br />Bottom line: VERY BAD I HATE.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1165844822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165844822" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1165844822?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165844822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10255548332858410596"><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>If you thought Queen Levana was evil before, you will see just how corrupted she <i>really is</i>! I don't often read novellas, but this one is a bit longer than average and completely worth it to be able to see Levana's childhood and how she grew up to be who she is. It also gives us a glimpse at our beloved characters' childhood so we get a real 360 look at what happened in the past. <br/><br/>Despite her evil ways and sometimes shocking delusions, Levana's story is just plain <i>sad</i>. This</span>
  <span id="freeText10255548332858410596" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars</b><br><br>If you thought Queen Levana was evil before, you will see just how corrupted she <i>really is</i>! I don't often read novellas, but this one is a bit longer than average and completely worth it to be able to see Levana's childhood and how she grew up to be who she is. It also gives us a glimpse at our beloved characters' childhood so we get a real 360 look at what happened in the past. <br><br>Despite her evil ways and sometimes shocking delusions, Levana's story is just plain <i>sad</i>. This hard-edged personality of hers was built from a tough childhood that lacked real parental guidance and, most importantly, love and affection. The fire tragedy that brought about her scars was horrifying, and some might consider it the beginning of the end. Having such a low self-image cost her a lot. She even becomes so deeply lost inside her own delusions that she's missed out on so much - love and happiness for one. Her craving what she thinks is love only makes her more blind to what she's actually denying herself - she's lost in a vicious circle of her own doings. It's sad and not entirely her fault, even, having grown up with a twisted view of love. I found this novella to be an incredibly in-depth and revealing look at her character. While I won't ever sympathize with her, it make us at least understand the "why" behind her actions, her wants.<br><br>Even though this novella is ultimately a character study, we also get to see the plot of the whole series take root. The virus sent to earth and her plan to blackmail, the beasts they're breading out of shells, the reason why some want to escape Luna - it just gives the whole series an extra layer of foundation. It's interesting to see that it doesn't all come from pure evil, there were some good intentions in Levana. If she attacked problems in a more… humane way, I'd even say she was a very good Queen for her people. She cares about her planet, about the future; her ways to reach her visions just happen to be quite… destructive. Like whoa!<br><br>I do recommend you read this one after you have read books 1-3, just so that it makes it all the more interesting. When you know the characters in the present, it's all the more fascinating to read about their past. But if you really wanted to read this one first it would still all make sense. You just wouldn't be able to appreciate all the connections, and the potential "spoilers" would probably not be noticed by someone who has no idea what's pertinent to the series. All in all, whether you're a fan of novellas or not, fan of the series should definitely read this one. I mean, is there anything better than an in-depth look at the villain of a story?<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388702323i/7905232.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10255548332858410596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_969286501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/969286501" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/969286501?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer969286501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1652130769206713474"><b>SO THIS WAS BASICALLY INCREDIBLE.</b> Am I suprised? nope. I've read 3 books by Marissa Meyer and they just get better and better (which is awkward since I rated <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_' title='Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinder</a> 5-stars and all the rest 5-stars so...I NEED MORE STARS, CLEARLY). I was so curious about this book because Levana (the villain of the series) didn't have a heck of a lot of development in previous books. She seemed like President Snow from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a>...really evil, but distantly so. I wasn't sure if <i>Fairest</i> would make me feel </span>
  <span id="freeText1652130769206713474" style="display:none"><b>SO THIS WAS BASICALLY INCREDIBLE.</b> Am I suprised? nope. I've read 3 books by Marissa Meyer and they just get better and better (which is awkward since I rated <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a> 5-stars and all the rest 5-stars so...I NEED MORE STARS, CLEARLY). I was so curious about this book because Levana (the villain of the series) didn't have a heck of a lot of development in previous books. She seemed like President Snow from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>...really evil, but distantly so. I wasn't sure if <i>Fairest</i> would make me feel sorry for her or hate her with a fiery passion. <br /><br />GUESS WHAT?! IT DID BOTH. <br /><br /><b>Fairest made me pity and loathe Levana all at once.</b> That takes incredibly wickedly <i>extraordinarily</i> amazing writing skills. I just bow to Marissa Meyer. I think she is a wizard or something.<br /><br /><b>The writing is gorgeous as usual!</b> I felt it took me 10 or so pages to really get into it...but I wasn't sure if it's because I haven't been in Lunar land for so long OR if the beginning felt draggy. <br /><br /><b>OHhhh, the ROMANCE IS CREEPY. </b> Like seriously. It's written so so well, that you can <i>nearly</i> see both sides. But Levana is downright creepy. At 15 she becomes obsessed with a palace guard and his offers of friendship are seen, in her eyes, as professions of love. It's a really miserable tale of brainwashing and manipulation and emotional torture. And since it's from Levana's eyes, I totally understood WHY she did it. But it freaked me out. She was a sociopath. <br /><br />Now <i>Fairest</i> IS a novella, and it's more of a prequel...but I think you could read it at any time (I wouldn't recommend reading it first if you haven't started The Lunar Chronicles yet. It wouldn't make sense.) But it's 222-pages and it's so so worth reading. I GAVE IT 5-STARS, DUH. GO READ IT.<br /><br /><b>THINGS YOU FIND OUT IF YOU READ FAIREST:</b><br />- How Levana got her scars <br />- Why she wears glamour<br />- Exactly what happened to Princess Selene<br />- Why Levana hates mirrors<br />- A few tidbits about Dr. Erland<br />- How Winter grew up (and who her real mother is)<br />- Why Levana is seriously twisted<br />- That Levana has an older sister, Channery (which you probably knew, but I'd forgotten until I read this)<br />- Why the Lunars decide to unleash that devastating disease on earth<br />- It has the first 3 chapters of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_" title="Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter</a> in the back (!!!!!!)<br />- What they eat on Lunar (this is very important and, obviously, delicious)<br /><br /><b>Why are you even still here?! YOU NEED TO READ THIS BOOK.</b> Incredible doesn't begin to cover it. It twisted me in a tangled knot of emotions and it's barely over 200-pages. I was so sucked into this book. I read it in a few hours flat and devoured the sample chapters of Winter. I NEED MORE. I need Winter. And while I pity Levana, I still hate her. She is a gloriously wicked villain with a completely tragic backstory and warped intentions. omg. This book is the best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1652130769206713474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1452889197" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1452889197" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8429172-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595453256p2/8429172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1452889197?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/8429172-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=damn-pretty-covers">damn-pretty-covers</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1452889197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13854375576952684676"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif' width='500' height='245' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Love is a conquest. Love is a war.<br/>Here is what I think of love.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>Blurb:</b> Mirror, mirror on the wall,<br/>Who is the fairest of them all?<br/>Queen Levana is a ruler who uses her “glamour” to gain power. But long before she crossed paths with Cinder, Scarlet, and Cress, Levana lived a very different story – a story that has never been told . . . until now. <br/><br/>Now this was interesting.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448737741ra/17182144.gif' width='500' height='282' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>As you may or may not, Levana is one of my favorite characters in the Lunar Chronicles series. I just enjoy reading her and wa</span>
  <span id="freeText13854375576952684676" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif" width="500" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Love is a conquest. Love is a war.<br>Here is what I think of love.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Blurb:</b> Mirror, mirror on the wall,<br>Who is the fairest of them all?<br>Queen Levana is a ruler who uses her “glamour” to gain power. But long before she crossed paths with Cinder, Scarlet, and Cress, Levana lived a very different story – a story that has never been told . . . until now. <br><br>Now this was interesting.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448737741ra/17182144.gif" width="500" height="282" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As you may or may not, Levana is one of my favorite characters in the Lunar Chronicles series. I just enjoy reading her and watching her plotting and being just nasty evil. So, learning how she became the queen she is now was a tricky trip.<br><br>I tend to have a soft spot for villains and while I enjoy them, I never wish they win.<br><br>That’s what happens with Levana.<br><br>When we read her earlier years as a princess, it’s inevitable not to pity her. Her sister, Crowned Princess and rightful queen Channary, was such a cruel bitch to her. Like, I can totally respect ambition when it’s laced with cleverness but Channary’s ambition was kinda misplaced. She wanted to be queen, she wanted to be the most beautiful queen Luna had ever had…. And then what? I honestly didn’t get much of her personality but being selfish, careless and cruel. She didn’t want to get <i>that</i> involved in the job she had to do which proved her weak. She was meant to be a weak queen. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448737741ra/17182145.gif" width="426" height="205" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Levana and I agreed on that.<br><br>Levana was the right queen for Luna but things didn’t work out that well.<br><br>While it’s true that Levana didn’t want to be as cruel as her sister, <i>who pushed her to pyre</i>, she couldn’t help but comparing herself to her and to everyone else. She’s traumatized by her older sister, often being the focus of her attacks and without being able to do anything about it but endure it silently.<br><br>It’s really hard to think of <i>this</i> Levana as the evil queen we all know when she isn’t half as bad but shit happens and while she chose, at the beginning, not to be like her sister, her own heart betrayed her and her ambition grew and grew until she was able to pretty much ripped her own heart out to get she wanted.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448737741ra/17182146.gif" width="300" height="184" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She was a very lonely girl who didn’t know what love truly was and all her life she’s been with her “glamour” on, making her look nothing like her scarred self at all, the only love she could find was a manipulative one. While I firmly believe she loved her husband, she didn’t love herself at all. She didn’t even know herself! I guess it’s difficult to remember who you are when you don’t look like you feel you do. So, what’s Levana?<br><br>Is she the offspring of a very lonely childhood with equal parts of humiliation and pain? Or is she the evil heart she always had?<br><br>I think it’s a combination of both. Do I think she could’ve been someone else? Someone better? <u>Absolutely </u> but she chose what she chose and that will be her doom.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13854375576952684676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1563775723" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1563775723" />
    <a title="Bangadybangz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39123161-bangadybangz"><img alt="Bangadybangz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424357545p2/39123161.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1563775723?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bangadybangz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bangadybangz" href="/user/show/39123161-bangadybangz">Bangadybangz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1563775723&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1563775723" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14193488960460192470">Omg... I'm feeling so many emotions right now and it's absurdly late, and I'm just trying to process it all. Wow. That was intense.<br/><br/>So I debated whether I was going to give this three stars or four, mostly because... this is not a happy read. But then I reminded myself that any piece of writing with can evoke the depth of feeling that this little book did for me is just good writing. So, hence the four stars.<br/><br/>I just feel so sorry for everyone in this story! Except for Channary. That hussy is strai</span>
  <span id="freeText14193488960460192470" style="display:none">Omg... I'm feeling so many emotions right now and it's absurdly late, and I'm just trying to process it all. Wow. That was intense.<br /><br />So I debated whether I was going to give this three stars or four, mostly because... this is not a happy read. But then I reminded myself that any piece of writing with can evoke the depth of feeling that this little book did for me is just good writing. So, hence the four stars.<br /><br />I just feel so sorry for everyone in this story! Except for Channary. That hussy is straight up evil. Mostly I just feel really really sad for Evret! He was so honorable and always wanted to do the right thing and he loved his wife and his daughter so much and it was just so heart breaking to see Levana manipulating and tormenting him the way she did. I just kept screaming at her to leave him alone and let him go be with his daughter and find happiness somewhere.<br /><br />Jeez Levana is frustrating. Like I understand her a little more now and why she's the way that she is, and I can sympathize a little bit, but I still do t like her. She is a scary, delusional psychopath with way too much power. <br /><br />So, with all that being said, while this wasn't exactly an "enjoyable" read for me, I feel it was a valuable one. It stirred a lot of emotions within me and has given me a lot to think about, and it's still a beautifully crafted story. And I did feel some twinges of excitement at all the little Easter eggs with the characters that I've grown familiar with from the rest of the Lunar Chronicles. <br /><br />And the scene where little Cinder was burned alive in the nursery... Damn that was rough. I'm glad we got a full explanation of what happened to her, but damn. And yet, I think the scene where Channary forced Levana to burn herself with mind control was even worse. Again, EVIL. <br /><br />Anyway, I'm going to try to get some sleep now. Wish me luck. Tomorrow... Winter is coming. =D<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14193488960460192470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3227101049" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3227101049" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

Unfortunately, I think her own spirit and natural characteristics allowed her to transform into what she did, which was a vengeful and brutal ruler.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1598462651ra/30019658.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I think this makes a fantastic piece of supplemental literature for anyone who is a big fan of the <i>Lunar Chronicles</i> series.<br><br>I had a lot of fun getting more information on this world and I am looking forward to reading <i>Stars Above</i> as well!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1598462834ra/30019675.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

But I just loved <i>Winter</i>.<br/><br/>Marissa Meyer demonstrates again how she can build fantastic worlds and interesting characters from nothing. It was intriguing reading about the Lunar world, especially from the bad guys POV. Even though it did not make Levana more sympathetic. Just more pathetic, naive, self-centered and cruel.<br/><br/>The thing is, I did not really </span>
  <span id="freeText11217587626589996284" style="display:none"><i>“Levana knew a great deal about beauty, just as she knew a great deal about ugliness.”</i><br /><br />I liked reading <i> Fairest </i> to pass the time waiting for <i>Winter</i>. But I just loved <i>Winter</i>.<br /><br />Marissa Meyer demonstrates again how she can build fantastic worlds and interesting characters from nothing. It was intriguing reading about the Lunar world, especially from the bad guys POV. Even though it did not make Levana more sympathetic. Just more pathetic, naive, self-centered and cruel.<br /><br />The thing is, I did not really need this novel in my life. I would have preferred reading the final installment at that time. Especially because it made the mysterious and evil Queen Levana less mysterious (but not less evil) and took some of my curiosity for Luna away.<br /><br />All in all, I still really liked it.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30510075-andie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30510075-andie?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106987865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7415772875814414873">It's official, Levana is bat shit crazy! Off her damn rocker. Needs to be locked up. Insane. Think that about sums it up. <br/><br/>I'm actually really torn about how I feel about this book. I went into it thinking I was going to get a backstory and then in turn understand why Levana is the way she is. And while I did get the reasoning behind it I still don't feel she is justified in any way and I absolutely do not feel sorry for her. Instead my heart actually hurts for those who have been so unfortunate </span>
  <span id="freeText7415772875814414873" style="display:none">It's official, Levana is bat shit crazy! Off her damn rocker. Needs to be locked up. Insane. Think that about sums it up. <br /><br />I'm actually really torn about how I feel about this book. I went into it thinking I was going to get a backstory and then in turn understand why Levana is the way she is. And while I did get the reasoning behind it I still don't feel she is justified in any way and I absolutely do not feel sorry for her. Instead my heart actually hurts for those who have been so unfortunate to ever cross paths with the crazy woman. She feels no remorse for anything that she's done and suffers from constantly wanting more and more, fueling her cruelty. <br /><br />Is this story a necessary read to fully enjoy the rest of the series? No I don't think so. But I did fully enjoy being inside Levana's twisted mind nonetheless. It's a great addition for any Lunartic and Marissa Meyer's writing is superb as always! </span>

<div id="review_2076052709" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2076052709" />
    <a title="Jiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana"><img alt="Jiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540380229p2/10502567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2076052709?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jiana" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana">Jiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781250068743" href="/book/show/22561230-fairest">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2076052709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11603123224605015445">Honestly, Fairest <u>blew me away.</u><br/><br/>After reading Cress two months ago and getting highly disappointed by it, my excitement for Winter decreased. I wasn't even planning on reading Fairest. However, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/57334157-caitlin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cait</a> recommended it to me after I told her I was looking for something short and easy to read and told me it was fantastic. Naturally, after Cress, I was a tad hesitant but I still decided to give it a try. And would you look at that! <b>Blown away!!</b> <br/><br/>Prior to starting this, I was aware I'd get to see the exte</span>
  <span id="freeText11603123224605015445" style="display:none">Honestly, Fairest <u>blew me away.</u><br /><br />After reading Cress two months ago and getting highly disappointed by it, my excitement for Winter decreased. I wasn't even planning on reading Fairest. However, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/57334157-caitlin" rel="nofollow noopener">Cait</a> recommended it to me after I told her I was looking for something short and easy to read and told me it was fantastic. Naturally, after Cress, I was a tad hesitant but I still decided to give it a try. And would you look at that! <b>Blown away!!</b> <br /><br />Prior to starting this, I was aware I'd get to see the extent of just how insane Levana is, but I was also told I'd feel sorry for her at some point. Yes, I felt sorry for her early on, then I hated her again as the novella progressed. And yes, I got to see just how much of a psycho she is. But now I <i>know</i> why she's the psycho she is, you <i>understand</i> (but not necessarily accept) why she's the way she is. She's so multilayered, it actually shocked me since we don't always get villains who are that developed. So, kudos to Meyer for creating such a complex villain!<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“She cried for the girl who had never belonged. A girl who tried so hard, harder than anyone else, and still never had anything to show for it.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />So far... Fairest is my most favorite of the series. It actually reminded me that I indeed love The Lunar Chronicles. And since Fairest offers background info on Selene and Winter, it got me super excited for Winter again. <br /><br />Levana, having grown up in the shadow of her mean sister Channary and without the love she needed from her parents, slowly turned into the horrible, crazy Levana we know now. We see all the inner thoughts of Levana and all the messed up, psychotic ideas that come to her mind. We also come to see how she lacks self confidence and she hides it well and that manifests in her need to control and manipulate everyone... My heart broke and I had tears in my tears over what she did to her first husband. It was absolutely heart breaking and I hated Levana for it, in addition to a bunch of other messed up things which solidified my hate for her. <br /><br />I know some people say it doesn't matter if you read this novella before or after Winter, but I highly recommend you do read it before Winter as it gives background history for Winter and it gets you really excited for the book (if you aren't excited already!). I absolutely can't wait for Winter!!!<br /><br />••• <b>Buddy read</b> with my fellow parrot lover, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61624004-amy" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy</a> ♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="11603123224605015445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1025990549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025990549" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025990549?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025990549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6939080797478643436"><b>Re-reading because I have just enough time to fit in this craziness before <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_' title='Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Winter</a></b> <br/><br/>Okay....bumped up 1/2 star because it is brilliant even if it is difficult to be in Levana's head for that long. She is <b>BAT-SHIT-CRAZY</b> and I understand how every step and decision she made from the time she was 15 led her to that last cruel step she took and rationalized to herself. She is so broken there is no chance of redemption anywhere.<br/><br/>*sobs for Evret*<br/><br/>First Read Jan 2015<br/><br/><b>3.5 Self Loathing Stars</b><br/><br/>The best villains</span>
  <span id="freeText6939080797478643436" style="display:none"><b>Re-reading because I have just enough time to fit in this craziness before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_" title="Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter</a></b> <br /><br />Okay....bumped up 1/2 star because it is brilliant even if it is difficult to be in Levana's head for that long. She is <b>BAT-SHIT-CRAZY</b> and I understand how every step and decision she made from the time she was 15 led her to that last cruel step she took and rationalized to herself. She is so broken there is no chance of redemption anywhere.<br /><br />*sobs for Evret*<br /><br />First Read Jan 2015<br /><br /><b>3.5 Self Loathing Stars</b><br /><br />The best villains are the ones that can rationalize and don’t believe they are the bad person, the ones that in a way you can sympathize with. After reading this I definitely understand the level of crazy Levana has going on in her head now. I can’t really say I sympathize with her BUT…I totally understand her better now and she is cray-cray.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> Love is a conquest.<br />Love is a war. <br />Here is what I think of love</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />It is uncomfortable to be in Levana’s head as she mistakes common niceties for love and as she reads far too much into the actions of others. <b>The first time she used her gift to get what she wanted from someone else</b> was horrifying at the same time it might have been understandable given her age but I still felt so bad for the person involved. The way she forced Evret into marrying her and the way she hurt him every day without even realizing it made it abundantly clear she doesn’t understand emotions the way a normal person would.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> Waiting would be agony. She would have to let him know that it was all right for him to mourn and love at the same time. She would not judge him, not when they were so clearly destined for each other</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Even though I did have a chance to see how her sister Channary tormented Levana and made her childhood practically unbearable it was still so hard to feel any true sympathy for her when what she did to Evert was so horrendous and tantamount to rape under the illusion of love.<br /><br />Levana’s madness grew over years from it being okay to poison an enemy with a plague, to forcing a person into an action against their will, to convincing yourself it is okay to murder a child, to stealing the throne, later glamouring more people and then later much much worse. She truly descended into madness.<br /><br /><b>I loved</b> getting glimpses of Winter as she is younger with Princess Selene and Jacin in the palace playing together as children. I’m really excited for what this means for the next book because Winter remembers her childhood even if Cinder does not.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> “Why is it always a prince?” asked Winter. “Why isn’t she ever saved by a top-secret spy? Or a soldier? Or a … a poor farm boy, even?” <br />“I don’t know. That’s just how the story was written.” Evret brushed back a curl of Winter’s hair. “If you don’t like it, we’ll make up a different story tomorrow night. You can have whoever you want rescue the princess.” <br />“Like a doctor?” <br />“A doctor? Well—sure. Why not?” <br />“Jacin said he wants to grow up to be a doctor.” <br />“Ah. Well, that’s a very good job, one that saves more than just princesses.” <br />“Maybe the princess can save herself.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I’m really excited for Winter since one of my favorite books of all times involves a crazy princess. Maybe our Winter could save herself.<br /><br /><b>Is this necessary to the rest of the series?</b> - Probably not. I did like getting some of Winters origins in this and seeing Levana’s PoV on the events of the past. Plus this story does clear up some of the speculation on how far Levana has gone to secure the Throne and which deaths she is responsible for. <br /><br />But if you like origin stories and enjoy knowing the motivations for characters then this is a great accompaniment to The Lunar Chronicles. <b>I do however suggest that you have read up through Cress so that nothing will be spoiled</b> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6939080797478643436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
